</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Java version history</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_8&amp;redirect=no" title="Java 8">Java 8</a>)</span></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><p>The <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java language</a> has undergone several changes since <a href="/wiki/Java_Development_Kit" title="Java Development Kit">JDK</a> 1.0 as well as numerous additions of <a href="/wiki/Class_(computer_science)" title="Class (computer science)" class="mw-redirect">classes</a> and packages to the standard <a href="/wiki/Library_(computer_science)" title="Library (computer science)" class="mw-redirect">library</a>. Since J2SE 1.4, the evolution of the Java language has been governed by the <a href="/wiki/Java_Community_Process" title="Java Community Process">Java Community Process</a> (JCP), which uses <i>Java Specification Requests</i> (JSRs) to propose and specify additions and changes to the <a href="/wiki/Java_platform" title="Java platform" class="mw-redirect">Java platform</a>. The language is specified by the <i>Java Language Specification</i> (JLS); changes to the JLS are managed under <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=901">JSR 901</a>.</p>
<p>In addition to the language changes, much more dramatic changes have been made to the <a href="/wiki/Java_Class_Library" title="Java Class Library">Java Class Library</a> over the years, which has grown from a few hundred classes in JDK 1.0 to over three thousand in J2SE 5. Entire new <a href="/wiki/API" title="API" class="mw-redirect">APIs</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Swing_(Java)" title="Swing (Java)">Swing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Java2D" title="Java2D" class="mw-redirect">Java2D</a>, have been introduced, and many of the original JDK 1.0 classes and methods have been <a href="/wiki/Deprecation" title="Deprecation">deprecated</a>. Some programs allow conversion of Java programs from one version of the <a href="/wiki/Java_(software_platform)" title="Java (software platform)">Java platform</a> to an older one (for example Java 5.0 backported to 1.4) (see <a href="/wiki/Java_backporting_tools" title="Java backporting tools">Java backporting tools</a>).</p>
<p>After the Java 7 release, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a> promised to go back to a 2-year release cycle.<sup id="cite_ref-oracle-curl_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oracle-curl-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> However, in 2013, Oracle announced that they would delay Java 8 by one year, in order to fix bugs related to Java <a href="/wiki/Computer_security_model" title="Computer security model">security</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Java 8 is the only publicly supported version, while after public support periods of older versions has ended, non-public updates have been issued for Java 7 and earlier.</p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="JDK_Alpha_and_Beta">JDK Alpha and Beta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: JDK Alpha and Beta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first alpha and beta Java public releases in 1995 had highly unstable <a href="/wiki/API" title="API" class="mw-redirect">APIs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Application_binary_interface" title="Application binary interface">ABIs</a>. The supplied Java web browser was named WebRunner.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="JDK_1.0">JDK 1.0</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: JDK 1.0">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first version was released on January 23, 1996 and called <b><a href="/wiki/Oak_(programming_language)" title="Oak (programming language)">Oak</a></b>.<sup id="cite_ref-pr10_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr10-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JavaHistory_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JavaHistory-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> The first stable version, JDK 1.0.2, is called Java 1.<sup id="cite_ref-JavaHistory_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JavaHistory-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="JDK_1.1">JDK 1.1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: JDK 1.1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Major additions in the release on February 19, 1997 included:<sup id="cite_ref-pr11_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr11-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>an extensive retooling of the <a href="/wiki/Abstract_Window_Toolkit" title="Abstract Window Toolkit">AWT</a> event model</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Inner_class" title="Inner class">inner classes</a> added to the language</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JavaBeans" title="JavaBeans">JavaBeans</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_Database_Connectivity" title="Java Database Connectivity">JDBC</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_remote_method_invocation" title="Java remote method invocation">RMI</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reflection_(computer_science)" title="Reflection (computer science)" class="mw-redirect">reflection</a> which supported Introspection only, no modification at runtime was possible.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Just-in-time_compilation" title="Just-in-time compilation">JIT (Just In Time) compiler</a> on Microsoft Windows platforms, produced for JavaSoft by Symantec</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Internationalization" title="Internationalization">Internationalization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> support originating from <a href="/wiki/Taligent" title="Taligent">Taligent</a><sup id="cite_ref-taligentau_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taligentau-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="J2SE_1.2">J2SE 1.2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: J2SE 1.2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Codename <b>Playground</b>. The release on December 8, 1998 and subsequent releases through J2SE 5.0 were rebranded retrospectively <b>Java 2</b> and the version name "J2SE" (<a href="/wiki/Java_Platform,_Standard_Edition" title="Java Platform, Standard Edition">Java 2 Platform, Standard Edition</a>) replaced JDK to distinguish the base platform from J2EE (<a href="/wiki/Java_Platform,_Enterprise_Edition" title="Java Platform, Enterprise Edition">Java 2 Platform, Enterprise Edition</a>) and J2ME (<a href="/wiki/Java_Platform,_Micro_Edition" title="Java Platform, Micro Edition">Java 2 Platform, Micro Edition</a>). This was a very significant release of Java as it tripled the size of the Java platform to 1520 classes in 59 packages. Major additions included:<sup id="cite_ref-pr12_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr12-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><code><a href="/wiki/Strictfp" title="Strictfp">strictfp</a></code> keyword</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Swing_(Java)" title="Swing (Java)">Swing</a> graphical API was integrated into the core classes</li>
<li>Sun's JVM was equipped with a <a href="/wiki/Just-in-time_compilation" title="Just-in-time compilation">JIT compiler</a> for the first time</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_plug-in" title="Java plug-in" class="mw-redirect">Java plug-in</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_IDL" title="Java IDL" class="mw-redirect">Java IDL</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Interface_description_language" title="Interface description language">IDL</a> implementation for <a href="/wiki/Common_Object_Request_Broker_Architecture" title="Common Object Request Broker Architecture">CORBA</a> interoperability</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_collections_framework" title="Java collections framework">Collections</a> framework</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="J2SE_1.3">J2SE 1.3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: J2SE 1.3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Codename <b>Kestrel</b>. The most notable changes in the May 8th, 2000 release were:<sup id="cite_ref-pr13_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr13-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ch13_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch13-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/HotSpot" title="HotSpot">HotSpot</a> JVM included (the HotSpot JVM was first released in April 1999 for the J2SE 1.2 JVM)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_remote_method_invocation" title="Java remote method invocation">RMI</a> was modified to support optional compatibility with <a href="/wiki/CORBA" title="CORBA" class="mw-redirect">CORBA</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_Naming_and_Directory_Interface" title="Java Naming and Directory Interface">Java Naming and Directory Interface</a> (JNDI) included in core libraries (previously available as an extension)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_Platform_Debugger_Architecture" title="Java Platform Debugger Architecture">Java Platform Debugger Architecture</a> (JPDA)</li>
<li>JavaSound</li>
<li>Synthetic proxy classes</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="J2SE_1.4">J2SE 1.4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: J2SE 1.4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Codename <b>Merlin</b>. The February 6th, 2002 release was the first release of the Java platform developed under the Java Community Process as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=59">JSR 59</a>. Major changes included:<sup id="cite_ref-pr14_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr14-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ch14_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch14-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Language changes
<ul>
<li><code><a href="/wiki/Assertion_(computing)" title="Assertion (computing)" class="mw-redirect">assert</a></code> keyword (specified in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=41">JSR 41</a>)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Library improvements
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Regular_expressions" title="Regular expressions" class="mw-redirect">Regular expressions</a> modeled after <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">Perl</a> regular expressions</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Exception_chaining" title="Exception chaining">Exception chaining</a> allows an exception to encapsulate original lower-level exception</li>
<li>Internet Protocol version 6 (<a href="/wiki/IPv6" title="IPv6">IPv6</a>) support</li>
<li>Non-blocking IO (named <a href="/wiki/New_I/O" title="New I/O" class="mw-redirect">New Input/Output</a>, NIO) (specified in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=51">JSR 51</a>)</li>
<li>Logging API (specified in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=47">JSR 47</a>)</li>
<li>Image I/O API for reading and writing images in formats like <a href="/wiki/JPEG" title="JPEG">JPEG</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics" title="Portable Network Graphics">PNG</a></li>
<li>Integrated <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> parser and <a href="/wiki/XSLT" title="XSLT">XSLT</a> processor (<a href="/wiki/JAXP" title="JAXP" class="mw-redirect">JAXP</a>) (specified in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=5">JSR 5</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=63">JSR 63</a>)</li>
<li>Integrated security and cryptography extensions (<a href="/wiki/Java_Cryptography_Extension" title="Java Cryptography Extension">JCE</a>, <a href="/wiki/JSSE" title="JSSE" class="mw-redirect">JSSE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_Authentication_and_Authorization_Service" title="Java Authentication and Authorization Service">JAAS</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_Web_Start" title="Java Web Start">Java Web Start</a> included (Java Web Start was first released in March 2001 for J2SE 1.3) (specified in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=56">JSR 56</a>)</li>
<li>Preferences API (<tt>java.util.prefs</tt>)</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Public support and security updates for Java 1.4 ended in October 2008. Paid security updates for Oracle customers ended in February 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-oracle2010_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oracle2010-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="J2SE_5.0">J2SE 5.0</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: J2SE 5.0">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Codename <b>Tiger</b>. The release on September 30, 2004 was originally numbered 1.5, which is still used as the internal version number. The number was changed to "better reflect the level of maturity, stability, scalability and security of the J2SE".<sup id="cite_ref-version_5_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-version_5-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> This version was developed under <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=176">JSR 176</a>.</p>
<p>J2SE 5.0 entered its end-of-public-updates period on April 8, 2008; updates are no longer available to the public as of November 3, 2009. Updates were available to paid Oracle customers until May 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Tiger added a number of significant new language features:<sup id="cite_ref-pr15_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr15-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ch15_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch15-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Generics_in_Java" title="Generics in Java">Generics</a>: provides compile-time (static) <a href="/wiki/Type_safety" title="Type safety">type safety</a> for collections and eliminates the need for most <a href="/wiki/Type_conversion" title="Type conversion">typecasts (type conversion)</a> (specified by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=14">JSR 14</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Metadata_(computing)" title="Metadata (computing)" class="mw-redirect">Metadata</a>: also called <a href="/wiki/Java_annotation" title="Java annotation">annotations</a>; allows language constructs such as classes and methods to be tagged with additional data, which can then be processed by metadata-aware utilities (specified by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=175">JSR 175</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Autoboxing" title="Autoboxing" class="mw-redirect">Autoboxing</a>/unboxing: automatic conversions between <a href="/wiki/Primitive_type" title="Primitive type" class="mw-redirect">primitive types</a> (such as <code>int</code>) and <a href="/wiki/Primitive_wrapper_class" title="Primitive wrapper class">primitive wrapper classes</a> (such as <code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/api/java/lang/Integer.html">Integer</a></code>) (specified by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=201">JSR 201</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Enumeration_(programming)" title="Enumeration (programming)" class="mw-redirect">Enumerations</a>: the <code>enum</code> keyword creates a <a href="/wiki/Type_safety" title="Type safety">typesafe</a>, ordered list of values (such as <code>Day.MONDAY</code>, <code>Day.TUESDAY</code>, etc.); previously this could only be achieved by non-typesafe constant integers or manually constructed classes (typesafe enum pattern) (specified by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=201">JSR 201</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Variadic_function" title="Variadic function">Varargs</a>: the last parameter of a method can now be declared using a type name followed by three dots (e.g. <code>void drawtext(String... lines)</code>); in the calling code any number of parameters of that type can be used and they are then placed in an array to be passed to the method, or alternatively the calling code can pass an array of that type</li>
<li>Enhanced <code><a href="/wiki/Foreach" title="Foreach" class="mw-redirect">for each</a></code> loop: the <code>for</code> loop syntax is extended with special syntax for iterating over each member of either an array or any <code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/api/java/lang/Iterable.html">Iterable</a></code>, such as the standard <code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/api/java/util/Collection.html">Collection</a></code> classes (specified by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=201">JSR 201</a>)</li>
<li>Improved semantics of execution for multi-threaded Java programs; the new <a href="/wiki/Java_memory_model" title="Java memory model">Java memory model</a> addresses issues of complexity, effectiveness, and performance of previous specifications<sup id="cite_ref-jsr-133_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jsr-133-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Static_import" title="Static import">Static imports</a></li>
</ul>
<p>There were also the following improvements to the standard libraries:</p>
<ul>
<li>Automatic <a href="/wiki/Method_stub" title="Method stub">stub</a> generation for <a href="/wiki/Java_remote_method_invocation" title="Java remote method invocation">RMI</a> objects</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Swing_(Java)" title="Swing (Java)">Swing</a>: New <a href="/wiki/Skin_(computing)" title="Skin (computing)">skinnable</a> <a href="/wiki/Look_and_feel#In_widget_toolkits" title="Look and feel">look and feel</a>, called <a href="/wiki/Synth_Look_and_Feel" title="Synth Look and Feel">synth</a></li>
<li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://java.sun.com/j2se/1.5.0/docs/guide/concurrency/overview.html">concurrency utilities</a> in package <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://java.sun.com/j2se/1.5.0/docs/api/java/util/concurrent/package-summary.html"><tt>java.util.concurrent</tt></a><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Scanner class for parsing data from various input streams and buffers</li>
</ul>
<p>Java 5 is the last release of Java to officially support the Microsoft Windows 9x line (Windows 95, Windows 98, Windows ME),<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Windows_Vista" title="Windows Vista">Windows Vista</a> is the newest version of Windows that J2SE 5 was supported on prior to Java 5 going end of life in October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-oracle2010_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oracle2010-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Java 5 Update 5 (1.5.0_05) is the last release of Java to work without any problems on <a href="/wiki/Windows_NT_4.0" title="Windows NT 4.0">Windows NT 4.0</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Java 5 is the default version of Java installed on Apple Mac OS X 10.5 (Leopard). Java 6 can be installed and set as the default to be used on 64-bit (Core <b>2</b> Duo and higher) processor machines.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Java 6 is also supported by 32-bit machines running Mac OS X 10.6 (Snow Leopard).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Java_5_updates">Java 5 updates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Java 5 updates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td>Java SE 5</td>
<td>2004-10-4</td>
<td>Metadata, generic types, autoboxing and auto-unboxing of primitive types, enhanced <code>for</code> loop, enumerated types, static import, formatted I/O, varargs, and concurrency utilities. Improved startup time and memory footprint. Sharing of read-only data between multiple running JVMs. Remote monitoring and management. A new JVM profiling API. Programmatic generation of stack traces. Support for XML 1.1 with Namespaces, XML Schema, SAX 2.0.2, DOM Level 3, and XSLT with a fast XLSTC compiler. Unicode 4.0 support.</td>

<td>Prior to this update, an applet or application could specify the version of the JRE on which it would run. This has changed. All applets are executed with the latest JRE version.</td>

<td></td>

<td>Java SE 5 Update 15</td>
<td>2008-03-06</td>

<tr>
<td>Java SE 5 Update 16</td>
<td>2008-07-23</td>
<td>This release fixes several security flaws, such as DoS vulnerabilities, buffer overflows, and other bugs which could lead to crashes or which would give applets access to certain system resources. These vulnerabilities were located in Java Web Start, in the Java Management Extensions (JMX) Management Agent, and in the functions for handling XML data.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 5 Update 17</td>
<td>2008-12-03</td>
<td>The UTF-8 charset implementation was updated to handle the non-shortest form of UTF-8 byte sequences, introducing an incompatibility from previous releases. New root certificates were added. Many bugs were fixed.</td>

<tr>
<td>Java SE 5 Update 18</td>
<td>2009-03-25</td>

<tr>
<td>Java SE 5 Update 19</td>
<td>2009-05-29</td>
<td>Support was added for several system configurations. Service Tag support was added. Many bugs were fixed, including several crashes and memory leaks.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 5 Update 20</td>
<td>2009-08-06</td>
<td>Several security vulnerabilities were resolved, such as potential system access by untrusted applets, and integer overflows in image processing and in Unpack200. Several new root certificates were added. Many other minor bugs were fixed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 5 Update 21</td>
<td>2009-09-09</td>
<td>Many minor bugs were fixed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 5 Update 22</td>
<td>2009-11-04</td>
<td>This release marks the End of Service Life (EOSL) for Java 5, and is its final public version. Several security vulnerabilities, reported as Sun Alerts 269868, 270474, 270475, and 270476, were fixed. Several other bugs were fixed. Furthermore, two new root certificates were added.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Java_SE_6">Java SE 6</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Java SE 6">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Codename <b>Mustang</b>. As of the version released on December 11, 2006, Sun replaced the name "J2SE" with <b>Java SE</b> and dropped the ".0" from the version number.<sup id="cite_ref-naming_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naming-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Internal numbering for developers remains 1.6.0.<sup id="cite_ref-version_6_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-version_6-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> This version was developed under <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jcp.org/en/jsr/detail?id=270">JSR 270</a>.</p>
<p>During the development phase, new builds including enhancements and bug fixes were released approximately weekly. Beta versions were released in February and June 2006, leading up to a final release that occurred on December 11, 2006.</p>
<p>Major changes included in this version:<sup id="cite_ref-pr16_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr16-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ch16_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch16-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Support for older Win9x versions dropped; unofficially, Java 6 Update 7 was the last release of Java shown to work on these versions of Windows.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This is believed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (November 2011)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to be due to the major changes in Update 10.</li>
<li>Scripting Language Support (<a href="/wiki/JSR_223" title="JSR 223" class="mw-redirect">JSR 223</a>): Generic API for tight integration with scripting languages, and built-in <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">Mozilla</a> <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> <a href="/wiki/Rhino_(JavaScript_engine)" title="Rhino (JavaScript engine)">Rhino</a> integration.</li>
<li>Dramatic performance improvements for the core platform,<sup id="cite_ref-lobby_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lobby-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-weblog_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weblog-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Swing_(Java)" title="Swing (Java)">Swing</a>.</li>
<li>Improved Web Service support through <a href="/wiki/JAX-WS" title="JAX-WS" class="mw-redirect">JAX-WS</a> (<a href="/wiki/JSR_224" title="JSR 224" class="mw-redirect">JSR 224</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_Database_Connectivity" title="Java Database Connectivity">JDBC</a> 4.0 support (<a href="/wiki/JSR_221" title="JSR 221" class="mw-redirect">JSR 221</a>).</li>
<li>Java Compiler API (<a href="/wiki/JSR_199" title="JSR 199" class="mw-redirect">JSR 199</a>): an API allowing a Java program to select and invoke a Java Compiler programmatically.</li>
<li>Upgrade of <a href="/wiki/JAXB" title="JAXB" class="mw-redirect">JAXB</a> to version 2.0: Including integration of a <a href="/wiki/StAX" title="StAX">StAX</a> parser.</li>
<li>Support for pluggable <a href="/wiki/Java_annotation" title="Java annotation">annotations</a> (<a href="/w/index.php?title=JSR_269&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="JSR 269 (page does not exist)">JSR 269</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Many <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">GUI</a> improvements, such as integration of <a href="/wiki/SwingWorker" title="SwingWorker">SwingWorker</a> in the API, table sorting and filtering, and true Swing <a href="/wiki/Multiple_buffering" title="Multiple buffering">double-buffering</a> (eliminating the gray-area effect).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_virtual_machine" title="Java virtual machine">JVM</a> improvements include: <a href="/wiki/Data_synchronization" title="Data synchronization">synchronization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Compiler" title="Compiler">compiler</a> performance optimizations, new algorithms and upgrades to existing <a href="/wiki/Garbage_collection_(computer_science)" title="Garbage collection (computer science)">garbage collection algorithms</a>, and application start-up performance.</li>
</ul>
<p>Java 6 reached the end of its supported life in February 2013, at which time all public updates, including security updates, were scheduled to be stopped.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Oracle released two more update to Java 6 in March and April 2013, which patched some security vulnerabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Java_6_updates">Java 6 updates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Java 6 updates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After Java 6 release, Sun, and later Oracle, released several updates which, while not changing any public API, enhanced end-user usability or fixed bugs.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> As of January 2016 Java 6 (and earlier) versions are no longer available for download from Oracle.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">

<th width="100">Release date</th>
<th>Highlights</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 6</td>
<td>2006-12-23</td>
<td>This release adds many enhancements in the fields of Web services, scripting, databases, pluggable annotations, and security, as well as quality, compatibility, and stability. JConsole is now officially supported. Java DB support has been added.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 6 Update 1</td>
<td>2007-05-07</td>
<td></td>

<td></td>

<td>2008-01-14</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/HotSpot" title="HotSpot">HotSpot</a> VM 10</td>
</tr>

<td>Java SE 6 Update 5</td>
<td>2008-03-05</td>
<td>Several security flaws were eliminated. New root certificates from AOL, DigiCert, and TrustCenter are now included.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 6 Update 6</td>
<td>2008-04-16</td>
<td>A workaround for the infamous Xlib/XCB locking assertion issue was introduced. A memory leak when using Kerberos authentication with LoginContext was fixed. Several other bugs were fixed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 6 Update 7<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td></td>
<td>Unofficially, Java SE 6 Update 7 (1.6.0.7) is the last version of Java that was shown to be working on the Win9x family of operating systems<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 6 Update 10<sup id="cite_ref-JSE6upd10_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JSE6upd10-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td>2008-10-15</td>
<td>HotSpot VM 11. Major changes for this update include:
<ul>
<li>Java Deployment Toolkit, a set of <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> functions to ease the deployment of <a href="/wiki/Java_applet" title="Java applet">applets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Java_Web_Start" title="Java Web Start">Java Web Start</a> applications.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Java Kernel, a small installer including only the most commonly used JRE classes. Other packages are downloaded when needed.</li>
<li>Enhanced updater.</li>
<li>Enhanced versioning and pack200 support: server-side support is no longer required.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Java Quick Starter, to improve cold start-up time.</li>
<li>Improved performance of <a href="/wiki/Java2D" title="Java2D" class="mw-redirect">Java2D</a> graphics primitives on Windows, using <a href="/wiki/Direct3D" title="Direct3D">Direct3D</a> and hardware acceleration.</li>
<li>A new <a href="/wiki/Swing_(Java)" title="Swing (Java)">Swing</a> <a href="/wiki/Look_and_feel" title="Look and feel">look and feel</a> called Nimbus and based on <a href="/wiki/Synth_Look_and_Feel" title="Synth Look and Feel">synth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Next-Generation Java Plug-In: applets now run in a separate process and support many features of Web Start applications.<sup id="cite_ref-6u10plugin_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6u10plugin-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 6 Update 11<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td>2008-12-03</td>
<td>13 security fixes<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 6 Update 12<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td>2008-12-12</td>
<td>No security fixes; 64-bit Java plug-in (for 64-bit web browsers only); <a href="/wiki/Windows_Server_2008" title="Windows Server 2008">Windows Server 2008</a> support; performance improvements of graphics and <a href="/wiki/JavaFX" title="JavaFX">JavaFX</a> applications</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 6 Update 13<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td>2009-03-24</td>
<td>7 security fixes, JNDI store and retrieve Java objects in LDAP slightly modified, JMX Change (createMBeanunregisterMBean), 4 new root certificates added</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 6 Update 14<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td>2009-05-28</td>
<td>HotSpot VM 14. This release includes extensive performance updates to the JIT compiler, compressed pointers for 64-bit machines, as well as support for the G1 (Garbage First) low-pause garbage collector.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
<p>The <b>-XX:+DoEscapeAnalysis</b> option directs the HotSpot <a href="/wiki/JIT_compiler" title="JIT compiler" class="mw-redirect">JIT compiler</a> to use <a href="/wiki/Escape_analysis" title="Escape analysis">escape analysis</a> to determine if local objects can be allocated on the <a href="/wiki/Stack-based_memory_allocation" title="Stack-based memory allocation">stack</a> instead of the <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_memory_allocation" title="Dynamic memory allocation" class="mw-redirect">heap</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Some developers have noticed an issue introduced in this release which causes debuggers to miss breakpoints seemingly randomly.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Sun has a corresponding bug, which is tracking the issue. The workaround applies to the Client and Server VMs.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Using the <b>-XX:+UseParallelGC</b> option will prevent the failure. Another workaround is to roll back to update 13, or to upgrade to update 16.</p>
</td>
</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Java_SE_7">Java SE 7 <span id="Java_7"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Java SE 7">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Java 7 (codename <i><b>Dolphin</b></i><sup id="cite_ref-JDK7_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JDK7-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>) is a major update that was launched on July 7, 2011<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> and was made available for developers on July 28, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> The development period was organized into thirteen milestones; on June 6, 2011, the last of the thirteen milestones was finished.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> On average, 8 builds (which generally included enhancements and bug fixes) were released per milestone. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://openjdk.java.net/projects/jdk7/features/">feature list at the OpenJDK 7 project</a> lists many of the changes.</p>
<p>Additions in Java 7 include:<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Java_Virtual_Machine" title="Java Virtual Machine" class="mw-redirect">JVM</a> support for <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_programming_language" title="Dynamic programming language">dynamic languages</a>, with the new <tt>invokedynamic</tt> bytecode under JSR-292,<sup id="cite_ref-JSR292_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JSR292-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> following the prototyping work currently done on the <a href="/wiki/Da_Vinci_Machine" title="Da Vinci Machine">Multi Language Virtual Machine</a></li>
<li>Compressed 64-bit pointers<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> (available in Java 6 with -XX:+UseCompressedOops)<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>These small language changes (grouped under a project named Coin):<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>
<ul>
<li>Strings in <a href="/wiki/Switch_statement" title="Switch statement">switch</a><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Automatic resource management in try-statement<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Improved <a href="/wiki/Type_inference" title="Type inference">type inference</a> for generic instance creation, aka <i>the diamond operator &lt;&gt;</i><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Simplified varargs method declaration<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Binary integer literals<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Allowing underscores in numeric literals<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Catching multiple exception types and rethrowing exceptions with improved type checking<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Concurrency utilities under JSR 166<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>New file <a href="/wiki/I/O" title="I/O" class="mw-redirect">I/O</a> library (defined by JSR 203) adding support for multiple file systems, file metadata and symbolic links. The new packages are <tt>java.nio.file</tt>, <tt>java.nio.file.attribute</tt> and <tt>java.nio.file.spi</tt><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Timsort" title="Timsort">Timsort</a> is used to sort collections and arrays of objects instead of <a href="/wiki/Merge_sort" title="Merge sort">merge sort</a></li>
<li>Library-level support for <a href="/wiki/Elliptic_curve_cryptography" title="Elliptic curve cryptography">elliptic curve cryptography</a> algorithms</li>
<li>An <a href="/wiki/XRender" title="XRender" class="mw-redirect">XRender</a> pipeline for Java 2D, which improves handling of features specific to modern <a href="/wiki/Graphics_processing_unit" title="Graphics processing unit">GPUs</a></li>
<li>New platform APIs for the graphics features originally implemented in version 6u10 as unsupported APIs<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Enhanced library-level support for new network protocols, including <a href="/wiki/Stream_Control_Transmission_Protocol" title="Stream Control Transmission Protocol">SCTP</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sockets_Direct_Protocol" title="Sockets Direct Protocol">Sockets Direct Protocol</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Upstream_(software_development)" title="Upstream (software development)">Upstream</a> updates to <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a></li>
<li>Java Deployment Rulesets<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Lambda (Java's implementation of <a href="/wiki/Lambda_(programming)" title="Lambda (programming)" class="mw-redirect">lambda functions</a>), Jigsaw (Java's implementation of <a href="/wiki/Modular_programming" title="Modular programming">modules</a>), and part of Coin were dropped from Java 7, and released as part of Java 8 (except for Jigsaw, which will be in Java 9).<sup id="cite_ref-JavaOne2011Keynote_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JavaOne2011Keynote-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jigsaw_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jigsaw-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Java 7 was the default version to download on java.com from April 2012 until Java 8 was released.<sup id="cite_ref-Java7AutoUpdate_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Java7AutoUpdate-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Java_7_updates">Java 7 updates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Java 7 updates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Oracle issued public updates to the Java 7 family on a quarterly basis<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> until April 2015 when the product reached the end of its support lifecycle.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th width="160">Release</th>
<th width="110">Release date</th>
<th>Highlights</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 7<sup id="cite_ref-JSE7_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JSE7-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td>2011-07-28</td>
<td>Initial release; <a href="/wiki/HotSpot" title="HotSpot">HotSpot</a> VM 21</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Java SE 7 Update 1<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
<td>2011-10-18</td>
<td>20 security fixes, other bug fixes</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Java_SE_8">Java SE 8</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Java SE 8">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Java 8 was released on 18 March 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> and included some features that were planned for Java 7 but later deferred.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Work on features was organized in terms of <a href="/wiki/JDK_Enhancement_Proposal" title="JDK Enhancement Proposal">JDK Enhancement Proposals (JEPs)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>JSR 335, JEP 126: Language-level support for <a href="/wiki/Lambda_(programming)" title="Lambda (programming)" class="mw-redirect">lambda expressions</a> (officially, lambda expressions; unofficially, <a href="/wiki/Closure_(computer_programming)" title="Closure (computer programming)">closures</a>) under Project Lambda<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> and default methods (virtual extension methods)<sup id="cite_ref-goetz_interface_evolution_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goetz_interface_evolution-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> which allow the addition of methods to interfaces without breaking existing implementations. There was an ongoing debate in the Java community on whether to add support for lambda expressions.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> Sun later declared that lambda expressions would be included in Java and asked for community input to refine the feature.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> Supporting lambda expressions also allows the performance of <a href="/wiki/Functional_programming" title="Functional programming">functional</a>-style operations on streams of elements, such as <a href="/wiki/MapReduce" title="MapReduce">MapReduce</a>-inspired transformations on collections. Default methods allow an author of an API to add new methods to an interface without breaking the old code using it. Although it was not their primary intent,<sup id="cite_ref-goetz_interface_evolution_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goetz_interface_evolution-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> default methods also allow multiple inheritance of behavior (but not state).</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>JSR 223, JEP 174: Project <a href="/wiki/Nashorn_(JavaScript_engine)" title="Nashorn (JavaScript engine)">Nashorn</a>, a JavaScript runtime which allows developers to embed JavaScript code within applications</li>
<li>JSR 308, JEP 104: Annotation on Java Types<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Unsigned Integer Arithmetic<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>JSR 337, JEP 120: Repeating annotations<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>JSR 310, JEP 150: Date and Time API<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>JEP 178: Statically-linked JNI libraries<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>JEP 153: Launch <a href="/wiki/JavaFX" title="JavaFX">JavaFX</a> applications (direct launching of JavaFX application JARs)<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>JEP 122: Remove the <a href="/wiki/Java_virtual_machine#Generational_heap" title="Java virtual machine">permanent generation</a><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Java 8 is not supported on <a href="/wiki/Windows_XP" title="Windows XP">Windows XP</a><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> but as of JDK 8 update 25, it can still be installed and run under Windows XP.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> Previous updates of JDK 8 could be run under XP, but had to be installed after a forced installation by directly unzipping files from the installation executable.</p>
<p>From October 2014, Java 8 has been the default version to download from the official website.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Java_SE_9">Java SE 9<span id="Java_9"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Java SE 9">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At JavaOne 2011, Oracle discussed features they hope to have in a 2016 release of Java 9,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> including better support for multi-gigabyte heaps, better native code integration, and a <a href="/wiki/Self-tuning" title="Self-tuning">self-tuning</a> JVM.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> In early 2016 the release of Java 9 was rescheduled for March 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>JSR 294: Modularization of the JDK under Project Jigsaw (<a href="/wiki/Java_Module_System" title="Java Module System">Java Module System</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Jigsaw_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jigsaw-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>JSR 354: Money and Currency API<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>JEP 222: jshell: The Java Shell (a Java <a href="/wiki/REPL" title="REPL" class="mw-redirect">REPL</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>There are plans to add <a href="/wiki/Automatic_parallelization" title="Automatic parallelization">automatic parallelization</a> using <a href="/wiki/OpenCL" title="OpenCL">OpenCL</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oracle-curl_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oracle-curl-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Work is under way to make the Java implementation of <a href="/wiki/Reactive_Streams" title="Reactive Streams">Reactive Streams</a> part of Java 9: <a href="/wiki/Doug_Lea" title="Doug Lea">Doug Lea</a>, leader of <a href="/wiki/JSR_166" title="JSR 166" class="mw-redirect">JSR 166</a>, has proposed<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> a new Flow class<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> that will include the interfaces currently provided by Reactive Streams.<sup id="cite_ref-infoq_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infoq-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Java_SE_10">Java SE 10<span id="Java_10"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Java SE 10">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There is speculation of introducing objects without identity (value types),<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as moving towards 64-bit addressable arrays to support large data sets somewhere around 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-oracle-curl_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oracle-curl-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Implementations">Implementations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Java_version_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Implementations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/OpenJDK" title="OpenJDK">OpenJDK</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open_source_software" title="Free and open source software" class="mw-redirect">free and open source</a> implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Java_Platform,_Standard_Edition" title="Java Platform, Standard Edition">Java Platform, Standard Edition (Java SE)</a>.</p>
<p>Before OpenJDK, several <a href="/wiki/Free_Java_implementations" title="Free Java implementations">Free Java implementations</a> were made by companies and groups such as <a href="/wiki/Apache_Harmony" title="Apache Harmony">Apache Harmony</a>. <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> also provides Java implementations,<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/RedHat" title="RedHat" class="mw-redirect">RedHat</a> provides it through the <a href="/wiki/IcedTea" title="IcedTea">IcedTea</a> project: a <a href="/wiki/Software_build" title="Software build">build</a> and <a href="/wiki/System_integration" title="System integration">integration</a> project for <a href="/wiki/OpenJDK" title="OpenJDK">OpenJDK</a>.</p>

<li id="cite_note-197"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-197">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Stahl, Henrik (2014-07-11). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://blogs.oracle.com/henrik/entry/the_future_of_java_on">"Updated: The future of Java on Windows XP"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corporation</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2014-11-11</span></span>. <q><i>JDK 8 is not supported on Windows XP. Early versions of JDK 8 had known issues with the installer on Windows XP that prevented it from installing without manual intervention. This was resolved in JDK 8 Update 25. The important point here is that we can no longer provide complete guarantees for Java on Windows XP, since the OS is no longer being updated by Microsoft. We strongly recommend that users upgrade to a newer version of Windows that is still supported by Microsoft in order to maintain a stable and secure environment.</i></q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJava+version+history&amp;rft.aufirst=Henrik&amp;rft.aulast=Stahl&amp;rft.btitle=Updated%3A+The+future+of+Java+on+Windows+XP&amp;rft.date=2014-07-11&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fblogs.oracle.com%2Fhenrik%2Fentry%2Fthe_future_of_java_on&amp;rft.pub=Oracle+Corporation&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
